c-button--article-toolbar article-toolbar-bookmark-menu"><button aria-controls="article-toolbar-bookmark-toggletip" aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="true" aria-label="Bookmark this article" data-sophi-feature="article toolbar bookmark denied" data-sophi-label="Save for later" id="article-toolbar-bookmark-btn" type="button"><svg class="button-bookmark tgam-button__icon c-button__icon" width="16" height="16" role="img" aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" pointer-events="none"><use xlink:href="#bookmark"></use></svg><span class="tgam-button__content">Save for later</span></button><div aria-labelledby="article-toolbar-bookmark-btn" data-sophi-feature="bookmark menu" id="article-toolbar-bookmark-toggletip" role="menu" class="tgam-popover tgam-popover--no-arrow tgam-popover--align-left tgam-popover--position-bottom tgam-popover--theme-light tgam-toggletip tgam-toggletip--theme-light" style="--tgam-popover-arrow-offset:1.0625rem;--tgam-popover-border-width:0.0625rem" hidden=""><div class="tgam-popover__inner tgam-toggletip__inner"><div class="tgam-popover__body tgam-toggletip__body"><span class="tgam-toggletip__text">Please log in to bookmark this story.</span><a class="Button__StyledButton-sc-136o1ng-1 kvJBQd tgam-button tgam-button--text-grey text-gml-2 Toolbarstyles__LinkButtonStyled-sc-1rif7tm-0 fPbqwa" data-sophi-action="link" data-sophi-feature="bookmark" data-sophi-label="log in" href="https://sec.theglobeandmail.com/user/login?intcmp=bookmark" style="padding:var(--space-8)"><span class="tgam-button__content">Log In</span></a><a class="Button__StyledButton-sc-136o1ng-1 kvJBQd tgam-button tgam-button--text-grey text-gml-2 Toolbarstyles__LinkButtonStyled-sc-1rif7tm-0 fPbqwa" data-sophi-action="link" data-sophi-feature="bookmark" data-sophi-label="create free account" href="https://sec.theglobeandmail.com/user/register?intcmp=bookmark" style="padding:var(--space-8)"><span class="tgam-button__content">Create Free Account</span></a></div></div></div></div></div></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Xanadu Quantum Technologies Inc. said Wednesday it has entered negotiations with the Ontario and federal governments to secure up to $390-million in support as the Toronto company prepares to go public.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">It’s unusual for a company to announce a prospective government funding arrangement, including specific dollar amounts, at such an early stage. But the optics matter for Xanadu as it closes in on two key milestones.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Next week Xanadu will learn how much of a potential US$455-million in net cash it will secure in its go-public transaction – or if the deal proceeds at all. If it does, Xanadu will become the first Canadian technology company to go public on the Toronto Stock Exchange since 2021. </p><div class="c-ad--base l-media"></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">The deal, <a href="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-xanadu-quantum-technologies-public-tsx-nasdaq-spac-crane-harbor/" target="_self" rel="" title="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-xanadu-quantum-technologies-public-tsx-nasdaq-spac-crane-harbor/">struck last November</a>, would see Xanadu merge with Nasdaq-listed special purpose acquisition company (SPAC) Crane Harbor Acquisition Corp. <a href="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/investing/markets/stocks/CHAC-Q/" target="_self" rel="" title="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/investing/markets/stocks/CHAC-Q/">CHAC-Q</a> and cross-list on the TSX. Investors will vote next Thursday on the deal, which if approved, is expected to close this month.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Before that, Crane unit holders have until Tuesday morning to say if they want in or out of the deal, which comes at a period of extreme market and geopolitical instability.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">The SPAC financing comes in two parts. Private investors have committed to buy US$275-million of stock in the combined company. Ninety per cent of that is from new backers, including chip giant AMD, BMO Global Asset Management, CIBC Asset Management, MMCAP Ventures, Planet First Partners and Polar Asset Partners. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Up to another US$227-million would come from Crane which, like other SPACs, is a publicly traded shell company that has raised money on the promise of merging with another company within two years.</p><div class="c-ad--base l-media"></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">However, the SPAC money is refundable for Crane investors who don’t like the deal, which values the combined entity at US$3.1-billion.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">That redemption feature is a wild card in any SPAC combination. When Canadian-founded D-Wave Quantum Inc. <a href="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/investing/markets/stocks/QBTS-N/" target="_self" rel="" title="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/investing/markets/stocks/QBTS-N/">QBTS-N</a> merged with a SPAC in 2022, 97 per cent of unit holders in the latter redeemed. The remaining US$9-million didn’t cover deal costs, <a href="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-d-wave-infinity-machine-cash-crunch/" target="_self" rel="" title="https://www.theglobeandmail.com/business/article-d-wave-infinity-machine-cash-crunch/">initially leaving the company in a tight cash position</a> once it went public. Transaction expenses on the Xanadu-Crane tie-up are expected to be US$45-million. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">“We want to get out as many great news articles and stories about what Xanadu is doing to try and make sure that we can keep as much of that money as possible” from the SPAC, Xanadu founder and chief executive officer Christian Weedbrook said. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">The government funding deal if completed would support a Xanadu initiative to establish advanced semiconductor and photonic manufacturing capabilities in Canada. </p><div class="c-ad--base l-media"></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">“The Government of Canada is a strong supporter of Xanadu and its mission, as reflected in previous funding agreements, and we remain in close contact with the company as it continues to grow,” said Sofia Ouslis, a spokeswoman for federal AI Minister Evan Solomon, when asked about the prospective government funding. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Mr. Weedbrook told analysts last week Xanadu needed to raise US$1-billion to fund its goal of building a quantum computer-based data centre by 2030. Securing as much of the SPAC money as possible will help, as will the US$275-million private funding. Xanadu has previously raised US$250-million from investors during its 10-year life. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Xanadu is one of the leading developers of quantum computers, which unlike conventional systems don’t derive power from manipulating bits of information, but by tapping the peculiar properties of matter and light at microscopic scales. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">There are several ways to leverage these effects in a quantum computer, and no clear winner has emerged yet. But if proponents are right, quantum computers will be vastly more powerful than the world’s most advanced supercomputers and able to do calculations beyond the reach of conventional systems. That could open new applications in fields such as material science, drug discovery and financial forecasting. </p><div class="c-ad--base l-media"></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Quantum computers could also enable bad actors to pick the locks on cryptography algorithms that secure the world’s digital economy. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Canada was an early leader in quantum, and the federal government has indicated that supporting its homegrown industry is of national importance. Three companies – Xanadu, Photonic Inc. and Nord Quantique – are among 11 that have advanced to the second stage of a U.S. Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency competition challenging developers to show they can build a commercial-grade quantum computer by 2033. Last December, Ottawa committed up to $23-million apiece to those three (plus a fourth company that isn’t in the competition), matching money from DARPA. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">If companies in the DARPA process make it to the end, they could get another US$300-million from the U.S. agency. Canadian industry observers are pushing the government to match that.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Xanadu’s system performs calculations using packets of laser light connected by fibre optic networks. The method is different from other quantum computers whose chips need to be cooled to temperatures just above absolute zero (-273.15 C), to harness their quantum effects. Xanadu’s machines largely operate at room temperature.</p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Like others, Xanadu has marked its progress with a series of technical papers published in Nature and other top science journals. In 2022, it became the third group to announce one of its machines had achieved “quantum advantage” by performing a particular calculation in two minutes that would have taken a conventional computer seven million years. </p><div class="c-ad--base l-media"></div><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Last year, Xanadu unveiled a chip capable of performing quantum error correction, a measure seen as essential for reaching reliable performance for practical uses. The system is also built via a modular approach, making it easier to network and scale up than other systems. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Continued efforts to correct errors and improve performance remain a key challenge for Xanadu and its rivals – though that hasn’t deterred investors from pouring billions of dollars into the sector in the past two years. </p><p class="c-article-body__text text-pr-5">Xanadu has also developed open-source software called Penny Lane that has 35,000 active users across an array of quantum systems. </p></article><noscript>Please enable JavaScript to view this content.</noscript><div class="default__LayoutContainer-sc-1xbbe8p-0 bksSxI" id="c0f3IXZdRJMudcP"><section data-sophi-feature="article actions" class="default__StyledArticleAction-sc-ay3ebk-0 iMsbjs"><div class="Container__StyledContainer-sc-120iz31-0 jmQbqE Flex__StyledFlex-sc-12wslmv-0 fJQkqd article-actions-inline"><p class="default__StyledReportAnError-sc-ay3ebk-1 bZyOWl"><a href="https://globeandmail.my.site.com/helpcentre/s/report-an-error" class="text-gmr-4" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Report an editorial error</a></p><p class="default__StyledReportAnError-sc-ay3ebk-1 bZyOWl"><a href="https://globeandmail.my.site.com/helpcentre/s/contactsupport" class="text-gmr-4" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Report a technical issue</a></p><p class="default__StyledEditorialCode-sc-ay3ebk-2 fEUDGj"><a href="/about/editorial-code/" class="text-gmr-4">Editorial code of conduct</a></p></div></section><div data-fusion-lazy-id="f0fbVFuAv67AUL"><div class="c-comments-container u-hidden"></div></div><div id="barchart-story-tickers-custom" class="barchart-story-tickers-wrapper" data-sophi-feature="barchart story tickers custom"><h5 class="text-pr-4 mt-0 mb-8">Tickers mentioned in this story</h5><p class="text-gmr-4 mt-0 mb-16">Study and track financial data on any traded entity: click to open the full quote page.
